        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite as a promising anode candidate of K-ion batteries (KIBs) has been increasingly studied currently, but corresponding rate performance and cycling stability are usually inferior to amorphous carbon materials.  To protect the layer structure and further boost performance, tempura-like carbon/carbon nanocomposite of graphite@pitch-derived S-doped carbon (G@PSC) is designed and prepd. by a facile and low-temp. modified molten salt method.  This robust encapsulation structure makes their resp. advantages complementary to each other, showing mutual promotion of electrochem. performances caused by synergy effect.  As a result, the G@PSC electrode is applied in KIBs, delivering impressive rate capabilities (465, 408, 370, 332, 290, and 227 mA h g-1 at 0.05, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g-1) and ultralong cyclic stability (163 mA g-1 remaining even after 8000 cycles at 2 A g-1).  On basis of ex-situ studies, the sectionalized K-storage mechanism with adsorption (pseudocapacitance caused by S doping)-intercalation (pitch-derived carbon and graphite) pattern is revealed.  Moreover, the exact insights into remarkable rate performances are taken by electrochem. kinetics tests and d. functional theory calcn.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A sandwich nanocomposite composed of commercially available SnO and reduced graphene oxide as advanced anode materials for sodium-ion full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Xu; Liang, Hao-Jie; Zhao, Xin-Xin; Yu, Hai-Yue; Wang, Mei-Yi; Nie, Xue-Jiao; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry Frontiers</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the past years, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted much attention due to their potential application in large-scale energy storage.  However, for now, it is difficult for anode materials to achieve further practical application.  In this work, we designed a sandwich structure in which SnO nanoparticles were entrapped between the layers of reduced graphene oxide (SnO/rGO) via freeze drying.  The unique structure can not only offer a 3D carbon network but also relieve vol. expansion during discharge/charge processes.  When used as an anode material for SIBs, the material exhibits excellent rate capability and stable cycling performance.  It can be found that a reversible capacity of 132.3 mA h g-1 can be obtained even at a c.d. of 5 A g-1.  In addn., SnO/rGO shows a charge capacity of 109.5 mA h g-1 with a capacity retention of 70.62% after 1200 cycles at 4 A g-1.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Rate and Long-Cycle Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Enhanced Electrode Stability and Kinetics via Binder Adjustment</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gu, Zhen-Yi; Sun, Zhong-Hui; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Zhao, Xin-Xin; Zhao, Chen-De; Li, Shao-Fang; Wang, Xiao-Tong; Li, Wen-Hao; Heng, Yong-Li; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are heralded as promising candidates for grid-scale energy storage systems due to their low cost and abundant sodium resources.  Excellent rate capacity and outstanding cycling stability are always the goals for SIBs.  Up to now, nearly all attention has been focused on the control of morphol. and structure of electrode materials, but the influence of binders on their performance is neglected, esp. in cathode materials.  Herein, using Na3V2(PO4)2O2F (NVPOF) as a cathode material, the influence of four different binders (sodium alginate, SA; CM-cellulose sodium, CMC; poly(vinylidene fluoride), PVDF; and poly(acrylic latex), LA133) on its electrochem. performance is studied.  As a result, when using SA as the binder, the electrochem. performance of the NVPOF electrode is improved significantly, which is mainly because of the high water soly., rich carboxyl and hydroxyl groups, and high adhesive and cohesive properties of the SA binder, leading to the uniform distribution of active materials NVPOF and carbon black in electrodes, good integrity, low polarization, and superior kinetic properties of the NVPOF electrodes, as demonstrated by SEM, cyclic voltammetry, electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique.  More importantly, when coupled with a hard carbon anode, the fabricated sodium-ion full cells also exhibit excellent rate performance, thus providing a preview of their practical application.  This work shows that the battery performance can be improved by matching suitable binder systems, which is believed to have great importance for the further optimization of the electrochem. performance of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGquQ6OHRhnRKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liW53H7yh8bZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFaqsL3N&amp;md5=05df07ffb30e969349fb8ace3b65a713</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201909486"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rajagopalan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Demand for energy in day to day life is increasing exponentially.  However, existing energy storage technologies like lithium ion batteries cannot stand alone to fulfill future needs.  In this regard, potassium ion batteries (KIBs) that utilize K ions in their charge storage mechanism have attracted considerable attention due to their unique properties and are therefore established as one of the future battery systems of interest among the scientific community.  Nevertheless, the development and identification of appropriate electrode materials is very essential for practical applications.  This review features the current development in KIBs electrode and electrolyte materials, the present challenges facing this technol. (in the com. aspect), and future aspects to develop fully functional KIBs.  The potassium storage mechanisms, evolution of the KIBs, and the advantages and disadvantages of each category of materials are included.  Addnl., various approaches to enhance the electrochem. performances of KIBs are also discussed.  This review is not only an amalgamation of different viewpoints in literature, but also contains concise perspectives and strategies.  Moreover, the potential emergence of a novel class of K-based dual ion batteries is also analyzed for the first time.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqy8yUVK8AKorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liW53H7yh8bZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitFeks74%253D&amp;md5=f97e076af9207003f805ea2601ff1f3a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1039/D0TA06614A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bimetallic Sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 Hollow Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Liang; Gao, Xuanwen; Zhang, Bao; Ou, Xing; Zhang, Jiafeng; Luo, Wen-Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a heterojunction and introducing an interfacial interaction by designing ideal structures have the inherent advantages of optimizing electronic structures and macroscopic mech. properties.  An exquisite hierarchical heterogeneous structure of bimetal sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 hollow nanorods embedded into a nitrogen-doped carbon matrix is fabricated by a concise two-step solvothermal method.  The FeS2 interlayer expands in situ grow on the interface of hollow Sb2S3 nanorods within the nitrogen-doped graphene matrix, forming a delicate heterostructure.  Such a well-designed architecture affords rapid Na+ diffusion and improves charge transfer at the heterointerfaces.  Meanwhile, the strongly synergistic coupling interaction among the interior Sb2S3, interlayer FeS2, and external nitrogen-doped carbon matrix creates a stable nanostructure, which extremely accelerates the electronic/ion transport and effectively alleviates the vol. expansion upon long cyclic performance.  As a result, the composite, as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibits a superior rate capability of 537.9 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 and excellent cyclic stability with 85.7% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  Based on the DFT calcn., the existing constructing heterojunction in this composite can not only optimize the electronic structure to enhance the cond. but also favor the Na2S adsorption energy to accelerate the reaction kinetics.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte Engineering Enables High Stability and Capacity Alloying Anodes for Sodium and Potassium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Lin; Cao, Zhen; Wahyudi, Wandi; Zhang, Jiao; Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Cheng, Yong; Wang, Limin; Cavallo, Luigi; Anthopoulos, Thomas; Sun, Yang-Kook; Alshareef, Husam N.; Ming, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">766-776</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of sodium and potassium ion batteries with greater energy d. is gaining great attention.  Although recently proposed alloying anodes (e.g., Sn and Bi) demonstrate much higher capacity than classic carbon anodes, their severe capacity fading hinders their practical applications.  The failure mechanism has traditionally been attributed to the large volumetric change and/or their fragile solid electrolyte interphase (SEI).  However, herein a completely new concept and approach are presented based on electrolyte engineering to stabilize alloying anodes.  This approach results in unprecedented high capacity (&gt; 650 mAh g-1) and stability (&gt; 500 cycles) of alloying anodes by simply tuning the electrolyte compns., without the need for nanostructural control and/or carbon modification.  It is confirmed that the cation solvation structure, particularly the type and location of the anions in the electrolyte, plays a crit. role in alloying anode stabilization.  A new anionic and alloying anode reaction model is presented showing that the root cause of the capacity fading in these alloys is dictated by the properties of the anions and not only the vol. change or fragile SEI effect.  Our model elucidates the failure mechanism in alloying anodes and provides a new guideline for electrolyte design that stabilizes alloying anodes in emerging mobile ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvlve8l8FFQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDTyX1YlItOw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXisFWrtbg%253D&amp;md5=1aa8da1f21de6c9b41d98d19e371bb88</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201602733"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Transition-Metal (Fe, Co, Ni) Based Metal-Organic Frameworks for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt- and Cadmium-Based Metal-Organic Frameworks as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries and Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Caifu; Xu, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7160-7168</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two multifunctional metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) with the same coordination mode, [Co(L)(H2O)]n·2nH2O [defined as "Co(L) MOF"] and [Cd(L)(H2O)]n·2nH2O [defined as "Cd(L) MOF"] (L = 5-aminoisophthalic acid) have been fabricated via a simple and versatile scalable solvothermal approach at 85 °C for 24 h.  The relationship between the structure of the electrode materials (esp. the coordination water and different metal ions) and the electrochem. properties of MOFs have been investigated for the first time.  And then the possible electrochem. mechanisms of the electrodes have been studied and proposed.  In addn., MOFs/RGO hybrid materials were prepd. via ball milling, which demonstrated better electrochem. performances than those of individual Co(L) MOF and Cd(L) MOF.  For example, when Co(L) MOF/RGO was applied as anode for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), it retained 206 mA h g-1 after 330 cycles at 500 mA g-1 and 1185 mA h g-1 could be obtained after 50 cycles at 100 mA g-1 for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolytes and Interphases in Sodium-Based Rechargeable Batteries: Recent Advances and Perspectives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Eshetu, Gebrekidan Gebresilassie; Elia, Giuseppe Antonio; Armand, Michel; Forsyth, Maria; Komaba, Shinichi; Rojo, Teofilo; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000093</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  For sodium (Na)-rechargeable batteries to compete, and go beyond the currently prevailing Li-ion technologies, mastering the chem. and accompanying phenomena is of supreme importance.  Among the crucial components of the battery system, the electrolyte, which bridges the highly polarized pos. and neg. electrode materials, is arguably the most crit. and indispensable of all.  The electrolyte dictates the interfacial chem. of the battery and the overall performance, having an influence over the practical capacity, rate capability (power), chem./thermal stress (safety), and lifetime.  In-depth knowledge of electrolyte properties provides invaluable information to improve the design, assembly, and operation of the battery.  Thus, the full-scale appraisal of both tailored electrolytes and the concomitant interphases generated at the electrodes need to be prioritized.  The deployment of large-format Na-based rechargeable batteries also necessitates systematic evaluation and detailed appraisal of the safety-related hazards of Na-based batteries.  Hence, this review presents a comprehensive account of the progress, status, and prospect of various Na+-ion electrolytes, including solvents, salts and additives, their interphases and potential hazards.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGofTJQHxRfLdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lityIKOSfyWMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXmsVWrur8%253D&amp;md5=da4e158754e397377d3896e6a2bc627d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.scib.2020.01.018"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-coating-increased working voltage and energy density towards an advanced Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C cathode in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gu, Zhen-Yi; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Sun, Zhong-Hui; Zhao, Xin-Xin; Li, Wen-Hao; Yang, Xu; Liang, Hao-Jie; Zhao, Chen-De; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science Bulletin</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">65</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">One main challenge for phosphate cathodes in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is to increase the working voltage and energy d. to promote its practicability.  Herein, an advanced Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C cathode is prepd. successfully for sodium-ion full cells.  It is revealed that, carbon coating can not only enhance the electronic cond. and electrode kinetics of Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C and inhibit the growth of particles (i.e., shorten the Na+-migration path), but also unexpectedly for the first time adjust the dis-/charging plateaux at different voltage ranges to increase the mean voltage (from 3.59 to 3.71 V) and energy d. (from 336.0 to 428.5 Wh kg-1) of phosphate cathode material.  As a result, when used as cathode for SIBs, the prepd. Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C delivers much improved electrochem. properties in terms of larger specifc capacity (115.9 vs. 93.5 mAh g-1), more outstanding high-rate capability (e.g., 87.3 vs. 60.5 mAh g-1 at 10 C), higher energy d., and better cycling performance, compared to pristine Na3V2(PO4)2F3.  Reasons for the enhanced electrochem. properties include ionicity enhancement of lattice induced by carbon coating, improved electrode kinetics and electronic cond., and high stability of lattice, which is elucidated clearly through the contrastive characterization and electrochem. studies.  Moreover, excellent energy-storage performance in sodium-ion full cells further demonstrate the extremely high possibility of Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C cathode for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpj9wLHnzVNOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lityIKOSfyWMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXptVakt7c%253D&amp;md5=afa981ca75d2e0e9d4fc45c635af6ae0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1039/C9EE03250A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, R. W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Assembled Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> Mxene and N-Rich Porous Carbon Hybrids as Superior Anodes for High-Performance Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-assembled Ti3C2 MXene and N-rich porous carbon hybrids as superior anodes for high-performance potassium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Ruizheng; Di, Haoxiang; Hui, Xiaobin; Zhao, Danyang; Wang, Rutao; Wang, Chengxiang; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">246-257</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) are attracting increased attention because of their low cost and similar energy storage mechanism to lithium-ion batteries.  Considering the low structural stability and poor electrochem. redox reaction kinetics resulting from the large size of K+ (1.38 Å), we elaborately designed novel PDDA-NPCN/Ti3C2 hybrids as PIBs anodes via an electrostatic attraction self-assembly approach, while N-rich porous carbon nanosheets (NPCNs) are derived from metal-hexamine frameworks.  The coupled PDDA-NPCN/Ti3C2 hybrids with stacked structure and large sp. surface area could ensure intimate contact between Ti3C2 and the NPCNs to efficiently take advantage of both components and more accessible active sites.  The hybrids afford enlarged interlayer spacing and unique 3D interconnected conductive networks to accelerate the ionic/electronic transport rates.  Meanwhile, the robust hybrids contribute high chem. stabilities due to favorable tolerance to vol. change caused by phase transformations during the fast charge/discharge process.  DFT calcns. further indicate that the PDDA-NPCN/Ti3C2 hybrids efficiently reduce the adsorption energy of K+ and accelerate the reaction kinetics.  The hybrids possess a remarkable synergetic effect, leading to a high reversible capacity of 358.4 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 and long cycling stability of 252.2 mA h g-1 with only 0.03% degrdn. per cycle within 2000 cycles at 1.0 A g-1.  This work paves the way for further self-assembled coupled hybrids in energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrtpmQXgbNRbbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lityIKOSfyWMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitF2mu77O&amp;md5=899bf4ab82540b972d8f95baafa060d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/eem2.12059"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Research Progress of Anode Materials for Potassium-ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Chenglin; Zhao, Huaping; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">105-120</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The next-generation smart grid for the storage and delivery of renewable energy urgently needs to develop a low-cost and rechargeable energy storage technol. beyond lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  Owing to the abundance of potassium (K) resources and the similar electrochem. performance to that of LIBs, potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) have been attracted considerable interest in recent years, and significant progress has been achieved concerning the discovery of high-performance electrode materials for PIBs.  This review esp. summarizes the latest research progress regarding anode materials for PIBs, including carbon materials, org. materials, alloys, metal-based compds., and other new types of compds.  The reversible K-ion storage principle and the electrochem. performance (i.e., capacity, potential, rate capability, and cyclability) of these developed anode materials are summarized.  Furthermore, the challenges and the corresponding effective strategies to enhance the battery performance of the anode materials are highlighted.  Finally, prospects of the future development of high-performance anode materials for PIBs are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoewF1CtWjyQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lityIKOSfyWMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1Ohtb3L&amp;md5=e1f4cf3332d66cc51e0bcfb3ce6798d4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c08094"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CoSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanotubes as a Potassium-Ion Battery Anode with High Initial Coulombic Efficiency and Superior Capacity Retention</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yanzhen; Deng, Qiang; Li, Youpeng; Li, Yijuan; Zhong, Wentao; Hu, Junhua; Ji, Xiaohong; Yang, Chenghao; Lin, Zhang; Huang, Kevin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (KIBs) have gained significant interest in recent years from the battery research community because potassium is an earth-abundant and redox-active metal, thus having the potential to replace lithium-ion batteries for sustainable energy storage.  However, the current development of KIBs is critically challenged by the lack of competitive electrode materials that can reversibly store large amts. of K+ and electrolyte systems that are compatible with the electrode materials.  Here, we report that cobalt monochalcogenide (CoSe) nanoparticles confined in N-doped carbon nanotubes (CoSe@NCNTs) can be used as a K+-storing electrode.  The CoSe@NCNT composite exhibits a high initial Columbic efficiency (95%), decent capacity (435 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), and stability (282 mAh g-1 2.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles) in a 1 M KPF6-DME electrolyte with K as the anode over the voltage range from 0.01 to 3.0 V.  A full KIB cell consisting of this anode and a Prussian blue cathode also shows excellent electrochem. performance (228 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 after 200 cycles).  We show that the NCNT shell is effective not only in providing high electronic cond. for fast charge transfer but also in accommodating the vol. changes during cycling.  We also provide exptl. and theor. evidence that KPF6 in the electrolyte plays a catalytic role in promoting the formation of a polymer-like film on the CoSe surface during the initial activation process, and this amorphous film is of crit. importance in preventing the dissoln. of polyselenide intermediates into the electrolyte, stabilizing the Co0/K2Se interface, and realizing the reversibility of Co0/K2Se conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokXb_MDV6C_bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lityIKOSfyWMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXjsl2jsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=c6b15363e79b580eff0b9f6cc1fb0c33</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b16418"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding High-Energy-Density Sn4P3 Anodes for Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenchao; Pang, Wei Kong; Sencadas, Vitor; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus-based anodes for alkali metal-ion batteries are attractive due to their high theor.-specific capacity.  However, their poor electrochem. performance caused by relatively large vol. variations during cycling, low elec. cond., and severe electrolyte decompn. due to highly reactive phosphide surface hinder their potential applications.  Herein, we confine Sn4P3 in N-doped carbon fibers as anode for potassium-ion batteries with enhanced cycling stability and high rate capability (160.7 mA hr g-1 after 1,000 cycles at 500 mA g-1).  The Sn4P3 anodes undergo a sequential conversion (P to K3P11, K3P) and alloying (Sn to KSn) reactions with synergistic K-storage mechanisms.  Also, the electrolyte with potassium bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide salt can effectively suppress the dendrite growth in K stripping/plating, stabilize the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer, and avoid excessive side reactions, thus enhancing the electrode stability.  This work provides a feasible approach to overcome the durability bottlenecks of K-ion batteries through regulating dendrite growth and SEI formation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp1_FgJPqbCy7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lic1uPPR0ZeIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsFGjsL7M&amp;md5=234adb45903e96506aa8b7293427db07</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-021-3334-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sarkar, S.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Roy, S.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchically porous SiOx/C and carbon materials from one biomass waste precursor toward high-performance lithium/sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Wenyan; Xu, Donghui; Kuang, Shaojie; Wu, Ziqin; Hu, Hang; Zheng, Mingtao; Yu, Xiaoyuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Silicon (Si)-based materials have emerged as promising anode materials owing to the theor. capacity as high as 4200 mAh g-1 and satisfying working potential for lithium insertion.  However, silicon-based anode materials inevitably face the dilemmas of huge vol. variation and poor elec. cond.  In this study, three-dimensional (3D) hierarchically porous SiOx/C and carbon materials have been designed and fabricated from one renewable biomass precursor (i.e., bamboo shoot hulls) through low-temp. activated treatment and mildly aluminothermic redn.  The SiOx/C anode after pre-lithiation treatment achieves an initial discharge capacity of 1332 mAh g-1 and a high capacity of 1289 mAh g-1 after 400 cycles at 200 mA g-1 as anode electrode for half lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  When employed for full LIBs, the SiOx/C exhibits a specific capacity of 142 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C with prominent cyclic stability and exceptionally low vol. expansion.  Moreover, hierarchically porous carbons are also prepd. from the same precursor through activation of CuCl2 and further removal of SiO2, exhibiting excellent electrochem. performances for lithium/sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoiGEZZS3bTSLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lic1uPPR0ZeIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtlOkt7c%253D&amp;md5=a8d4e796af3ec7502eb68184569f05fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2020.126520"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chandra, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Devina, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alvin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">New Strategy for Increasing Sodium-Ion Uptake in Silicon Oxycarbides</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New strategy for increasing sodium-ion uptake in silicon oxycarbides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chandra, Christian; Devina, Winda; Alvin, Stevanus; Kim, Jaehoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">404</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">126520</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Silicon oxycarbides (SiOCs) are considered promising sodium-ion battery anode materials.  However, the total and low-voltage plateau capacities of SiOCs are low (below 200 and 95 mAh g-1, resp.), which hinders the manufg. of high-d. electrodes.  Herein a new strategy for improving the electrochem. performance of SiOCs was proposed by considering the Na+ ion storage mechanisms in SiOCs.  High-capacity SiOCs were synthesized by increasing the amt. of C- and O-rich SiOxCy phases and reducing the amt. of inactive SiO2, SiC, and Cfree phases.  The compns. of SiOCs were controlled by adjusting the synthesis conditions (e.g., sweep gas and pyrolysis time) and C content of the SiOC precursors.  The use of N2 sweep gas instead of H2/Ar suppressed the formation of SiC and Cfree.  In addn., the amt. of inactive SiO2 phase in SiOCs was further suppressed using a C-rich precursor.  Consequently, the synthesized SiOC, which was enriched with C- and O-rich SiOxCy phases, delivered a high reversible capacity of 234 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 25 mA g-1.  In const.-current/const. voltage mode, the reversible capacity was further increased to 299 mAh g-1, which was close to the theor. max. capacity of 315 mAh g-1.  After 140 cycles, the reversible capacity was stabilized to 160 mAh g-1.  The initial capacity loss during long-term cycling, which was mostly caused by the progressive decrease in the low-voltage plateau capacities, was attributed to the increase in cell polarization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoo1Lhu9_sv1bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lic1uPPR0ZeIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsFKgt7jJ&amp;md5=6feca10f7ee8063d57b9b57f3badd6e1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/inf2.12184"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-ionicity fluorophosphate lattice via aliovalent substitution as advanced cathode materials in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gu, Zhen-Yi; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Zhao, Xin-Xin; Wang, Xiao-Tong; Xie, Dan; Sun, Zhong-Hui; Zhao, Chen-De; Liang, Hao-Jie; Li, Wen-Hao; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">InfoMat</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">694-704</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">INFOHH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2567-3165</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons Australia, Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a cathode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) with 3D open framework is a promising candidate due to its high working voltage and large theor. capacity.  However, the severe capacity degrdn. and poor rate capability hinder its practical applications.  The present study demonstrated the optimization of Na-storage performance of NVPF via delicate lattice modulation.  Aliovalent substitution of V3+ at Na+ in NVPF induces the generation of electronic defects and expansion of Na+-migration channels, resulting in the enhancement in electronic cond. and acceleration of Na+-migration kinetics.  It is disclosed that the formed stronger Na O bonds with high ionicity than V O bonds lead to the significant increase in structural stability and ionicity in the Na+-substituted NVPF (NVPF-Nax).  The aforementioned effects of Na+ substitution achieve the unprecedented electrochem. performance in the optimized Na3.14V1.93Na0.07(PO4)2F3 (NVPF-Na0.07).  As a result, NVPF-Na0.07 delivers a high-rate capability (77.5 mAh g-1 at 20 C) and ultralong cycle life (only 0.027% capacity decay per cycle over 1000 cycles at 10 C).  Sodium-ion full cells are designed using NVPF-Na0.07 as cathode and Se@reduced graphene oxide as anode.  The full cells exhibit excellent wide-temp. electrochem. performance from -25 to 25°C with an outstanding rate capability (96.3 mAh g-1 at 20 C).  Furthermore, it delivered an excellent cycling performance over 300 cycles with a capacity retention exceeding 90% at 0.5 C under different temps.  This study demonstrates a feasible strategy for the development of advanced cathode materials with excellent electrochem. properties to achieve high-efficiency energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrT_2pDcsfe-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liQz0TRH_rF4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXitVymu7rO&amp;md5=40606b0c447d1aea02e1989ce5c8917c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1002/inf2.12101"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-based energy storage technologies, esp. potassium ion batteries (PIBs), have received great interest over the past decade.  A pivotal challenge facing high-performance PIBs is to identify advanced electrode materials that can store the large-radius K+ ions, as well as to tailor the various thermodn. parameters.  Metal chalcogenides are one of the most promising anode materials, having a high theor. specific capacity, high in-plane elec. cond., and relatively small vol. change on charge/discharge.  However, the development of metal chalcogenides for PIBs is still in its infancy because of the limited choice of high-performance electrode materials.  However, numerous efforts have been made to conquer this challenge.  In this article, we overview potassium storage mechanisms, the tech. hurdles, and the optimization strategies for metal chalcogenides and highlight how the adjustment of the cryst. structure and choice of the electrolyte affect the electrochem. performance of metal-chalcogenide-based electrode materials.  Other potential potassium-based energy storage systems to which metal chalcogenides can be applied are also discussed.  Finally, future research directions focusing on metal chalcogenides for potassium storage are proposed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3hx0ofIqCP7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liQz0TRH_rF4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVKntr7F&amp;md5=4cde84266838b581db83005bacb29bdf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202102280"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temp. sodium-sulfur (RT Na-S) batteries have attracted extensive attention because of their low cost and high specific energy.  RT Na-S batteries, however, usually suffer from sluggish reaction kinetics, low reversible capacity, and short lifespans.  Herein, it is shown that chain-mail catalysts, consisting of porous nitrogen doped carbon nanofibers (PCNFs) encapsulating Co nanoparticles (Co@PCNFs), can activate sulfur via electron engineering.  The chain-mail catalysts Co@PCNFs with a micrograde hierarchical structure as a freestanding sulfur cathode (Co@PCNFs/S) can provide space for high mass loading of sulfur and polysulfides.  The electrons can rapidly transfer from chain-mail catalysts to sulfur and polysulfides during discharge-charge processes, therefore boosting its conversion kinetics.  As a result, this freestanding Co@PCNFs/S cathode achieves a high sulfur loading of 2.1 ± 0.2 mg cm-2, delivering a high reversible capacity of 398 mA h g-1 at 0.5 C (1 C = 1675 mA g-1) over 600 cycles and superior rate capability of an av. capacity of 240 mA h g-1 at 5 C.  Exptl. results, combined with d. functional theory calcns., demonstrate that the Co@PCNFs/S can efficiently improve the conversion kinetics between the polysulfides and Na2S via transferring electrons from Co to them, thereby realizing efficient sulfur redox reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqW0B2T74CjxbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liQz0TRH_rF4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVegur3P&amp;md5=154bb3ddb85a951c6926e27ad986e6f2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201811080"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temp. sodium-sulfur (RT-Na/S) batteries hold significant promise for large-scale application because of low cost of both sodium and sulfur. As the key component, anode dets. their energy d. and safety.  Alloy-based anodes, such as P, Sn, Sb, and Bi, have attracted extensive attention due to their abundant resources, suitable working potentials, and large theor. capacities.  However, the dramatic vol. variation upon (de)potassiation results in pulverization of particles and their detaching from the current collector accompanied with performance decay.  Various strategies, including designing micro-/nanostructures, introducing carbon substrates, and optimizing electrode/electrolyte interface, have been demonstrated to effectively alleviate these issues.  Herein, we summarize the recent research progresses on alloy-based materials in KIBs.  The synthesis methods, electrochem. performance, reaction mechanisms, and structure-activity relationships of these materials are considered, and challenges and perspectives are provided.  This review provides new insight into designing of high-activity electrode materials for KIBs and beyond.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Incorporation of acetate-based ionic liquids into a zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-8) as efficient sorbents for carbon dioxide capture</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mohamedali, Mohanned; Ibrahim, Hussameldin; Henni, Amr</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tuning solid sorbent interior pores to improve their adsorption properties is considered an effective approach to enhance gas sepn. performance.  This work examd. improved CO2 capture performance of ZIF8-impregnated with ionic liq. (IL), 1-butyl-3-methylimidazolium acetate ([Bmim][Ac]) and 1-Ethyl-3-methylimidazolium acetate ([Emim][Ac]).  Synthesis and detailed characterizations of the composite materials are reported, and the effect of ionic liq. (IL) loading was studied.  Fourier transform IR spectroscopy confirmed the impregnation of IL into the ZIF-8 pores; thermogravimetric anal. assessed thermal stability of the composite materials.  Powder x-ray diffraction patterns of the IL@ZIF-8 samples showed the ZIF-8 crystal structure remained intact after impregnation.  BET surface area and pore vols. significantly decreased (up to 80%) for [Bmim][Ac]@ZIF-8 with a 30 wt. percent IL load, confirming the presence of IL inside the ZIF-8 internal pores.  CO2 and N2 adsorption isotherms of the IL@ZIF-8 composites were evaluated gravimetrically at 303, 313, and 323° K.  Impregnated samples exhibited substantially higher CO2 uptake and CO2/N2 selectivity at all studied temps. up to 7 times higher than the CO2 capacity at 0.2 bar and 303° K for [Bmim][Ac]@ZIF-30 vs. pristine ZIF-8.  Results provide insights for the synthesis, structure, and sorption capacity of these composite materials, which could be used to design sorbents with outstanding properties to meet environmental challenges.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoX-0HyhjPzubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoMDqTpL8fjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslaltrbL&amp;md5=0aefc3a0a9915057af72fd2b2d187373</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acscatal.7b03270"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoreactor of MOF-Derived Yolk-Shell Co@C-N: Precisely Controllable Structure and Enhanced Catalytic Activity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Huirong; Shen, Kui; Mao, Qing; Chen, Junying; Li, Yingwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Catalysis</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1417-1426</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACCACS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2155-5435</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow yolk-shell nanoreactors are of great interest in heterogeneous catalysis owing to their improved mass transfer ability and stability.  Here, the authors report a facile and straight route to synthesize a highly efficient and recyclable yolk-shell Co@C-N nanoreactor with controllable properties by the direct thermolysis of a hollow Zn/Co-ZIF precursor.  Based on systematical optimization of the pyrolysis temp. and the shell-thickness of Zn/Co-ZIFs, the authors could completely anchor and stabilize uniform Co nanoparticles (NPs) in the hollow yolk, accommodated by the Co-ZIF derived N-doped C nanosheets.  This nanosheet-assembled yolk was further confined by a permeable and robust N-doped C (C-N) shell to protect the Co NPs against leaching and also enabled the reaction to take place in the hollow void.  Consequently, the optimal yolk-shell Co@C-N nanoreactor showed a significantly enhanced catalytic activity for the aq. oxidn. of alcs., yielding &gt; 99% conversion under atm. air and base-free conditions, which was much higher than that of the solid counterparts derived from pure ZIF-67 and solid core-shell ZIF-67@ZIF-8 precursors (with 14% and 59% conversion under the same reaction condition, resp.).  The enhanced catalytic activity should be attributed to the yolk-shell structure that could facilitate the transport of reactant/product and the strong interaction between the Co NPs and N-doped C nanosheet to afford pos. synergistic effects.  Also, this catalyst also showed good recyclability, magnetically reusability, and general applicability for a broad substrate scope, further highlighting the structure superiority of the authors' yolk-shell nanoreactor.  This strategy might open an avenue to synthesize various hollow yolk-shell nanoreactors with controllable structures and enhanced catalytic performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHTlp1BXl_T7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoMDqTpL8fjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXlvVCnug%253D%253D&amp;md5=1bc71fe64e7201c8afc4506c2be1e908</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201701229"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Proton-conductive metal-organic frameworks: Recent advances and perspectives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Ai-Lin; Gao, Qiang; Xu, Jian; Bu, Xian-He</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Coordination Chemistry Reviews</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Over the past decades, research on proton-conductive metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) has rapidly accelerated due to the importance of energy for modern society.  This review mainly focuses on some representative proton-conductive MOFs reported recently, with related discussions on the underlying proton transportation mechanisms.  In the first section, authors give a brief introduction to the background of proton-conductive MOFs.  In the following second section, a summarization on the widely used exptl. characterization techniques as well as the well-established computational methods for exploring the proton transportation mechanism is given.  In the third section, some representative studies in this field are reviewed from the aspect that how to tune the proton cond. of MOFs, with emphasis on the following factors: the impact of framework and guest mols./ions; the modification with functionalized groups and the tuning of Bronsted acidity; the influence of phase transition, defects, and amorphization.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-Organic Frameworks for Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Ruo; Liang, Zibin; Zou, Ruqiang; Xu, Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) and their derivs. are two developing families of functional materials for energy storage and conversion.  Their high porosity, versatile functionalities, diverse structures, and controllable chem. compns. offer immense possibilities in the search for adequate electrode materials for rechargeable batteries.  Despite these advantageous features, MOFs and their derivs. as electrode materials face various challenging issues, which impede their practical applications.  From this perspective, we present both the opportunities and challenges that MOFs/MOF composites and MOF-derived materials bring to rechargeable batteries, including lithium-ion batteries, lithium-sulfur batteries, lithium-oxygen batteries, and sodium-ion batteries.  By discussing the development of MOFs/MOF composites and MOF-derived materials in each battery system, some design principles that dominate the specific electrochem. behaviors are outlined, with the key requirements that a practical electrode should fulfill.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure Types and Magnetic Behavior of Cobalt Nanoclusters</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liao, Beiling; Li, Shixiong; Yang, Guoping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Caprylic hydrazide ligands are ideal ligands for the synthesis of novel polynuclear metal complexes, because they contain many N,O coordination atoms with a strong coordination ability, abundant H-bond donors, acceptors, and large conjugation systems.  One dodecanuclear Co nanocluster [CoII8CoIII4(L1)4(Py)12(MeOH)4(AcO)4]·(MeOH)13 (1) and 1 octadecanuclear Co nanocluster [CoII18(L2)6(Py)48]·(DMF)5·(MeOH)8 (2) were obtained by using H6L1 and H6L2 ligands, resp. (Py = pyridine).  The cyclic Co nanocluster 1 can be regarded as 2 pentanuclear Co units (Co5(N-N)4) connected by 2 Co ions, and it is a mixed-valent Co nanocluster.  Every H6L1 ligand contains 10 coordination atoms, each of which coordinates with the Co ions.  Every 2 H6L1 ligands form a structure similar to a handshake.  The abnormal cylindrical Co nanocluster 2 can be regarded 6 trinuclear Co units Co3(N-N)2 connected by 1 L26- ligand, and every L26- ligand splits the structure on both sides, with a twisted cyclohexane in the middle.  AC magnetic susceptibilities show that nanocluster 1 exhibits no frequency-dependent behavior, but nanocluster 2 shows a single-mol. magnetic behavior, and the relaxation process of the energy barrier is 20.4 K.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGptWxbqY63i2LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHM38wUYPq8Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXht1eqtrc%253D&amp;md5=efaa65a9b44798ed8b994634e3c237e3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.06.009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interplanar space-controllable carboxylate pillared metal organic framework ultrathin nanosheet for superhigh capacity rechargeable alkaline battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Junpeng; Zhao, Hongyang; Wang, Jianwei; Li, Na; Wu, Miaomiao; Zhang, Qian; Du, Yaping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">62</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hydroxides and their derivs. as cathode materials of rechargeable alk. batteries have limited specific capacity.  In this work, a new ultrathin metal org. framework (MOF) nanosheet with expanded interplanar space is delicately designed.  The org. ligand as a pillar enlarges the interplanar space for ion transportation to Ni/Co redox centers.  The obtained NiCo-MOF cathode has high capacity and rate retention, specifically, 225 mAh g-1 and 82% capacity retention from 1 to 20 A g-1, which is over four-fold to that of NiCo-LDH.  A full cell composed of NiCo-MOF cathode and an org. anode shows high capacity of 280 mAh g-1 with long-term cycle stability.  Furthermore, we find electrochem. performance increases linearly with larger interplanar space.  The present results can give new insight into structure design for advanced cathode materials and understanding the relationship between structures and performance of alk. batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvNtEK64MDz7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHM38wUYPq8Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXht1alsbbI&amp;md5=42310e859f237370ce0df730557bc06e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.8b06020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, D.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stabilization of Hexaaminobenzene in a 2D Conductive Metal-Organic Framework for High Power Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Jihye; Lee, Minah; Feng, Dawei; Huang, Zhehao; Hinckley, Allison C.; Yakovenko, Andrey; Zou, Xiaodong; Cui, Yi; Bao, Zhenan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Redox-active org. materials have gained growing attention as electrodes of rechargeable batteries.  However, their key limitations are the low electronic cond. and limited chem. and structural stability under redox conditions.  Herein, a new cobalt-based 2D conductive metal-org. framework (MOF), Co-HAB, having stable, accessible, dense active sites is reported for high-power energy storage device through conjugative coordination between a redox-active linker, hexaaminobenzene (HAB), and a Co(II) center.  Given the exceptional capability of Co-HAB for stabilizing reactive HAB, a reversible three-electron redox reaction per HAB was successfully demonstrated for the first time, thereby presenting a promising new electrode material for sodium-ion storage.  Specifically, through synthetic tunability of Co-HAB, the bulk elec. cond. of 1.57 S cm-1 was achieved, enabling an extremely high rate capability, delivering 214 mAh g-1 within 7 min or 152 mAh g-1 in 45 s.  Meanwhile, an almost linear increase of the areal capacity upon increasing active mass loading up to 9.6 mg cm-2 was obtained, demonstrating 2.6 mAh cm-2 with a trace amt. of conducting agent.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWskywUxC3zrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHM38wUYPq8Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlyktbzP&amp;md5=3718ffcfee4d8e1d925eb40c252f7abc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2020.06.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, J.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interface Engineering between the Metal-Organic Framework Nanocrystal and Graphene toward Ultrahigh Potassium-Ion Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Peitao; Li, Shuo; Yu, Chengbing; Wang, Ying; Xu, Yuxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10210-10218</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The potassium-ion battery (PIB) has been recognized as a promising low-cost and high-energy battery; however, it suffers from a relatively low capacity and inferior cycling performance compared with current electrode materials.  Herein, we report an effective interface engineering strategy to prep. metal-org. framework (MOF) nanocrystals tightly encapsulated by reduced graphene oxide (rGO) via strong chem. interaction as a free-standing anode for PIB.  Based on exptl. anal. and theor. calcns., we systematically investigated the effect of the chem.-bonded interface between MOF nanocrystals and conductive rGO and revealed that the strong chem. interface can substantially enhance the adsorption energy and ion transport kinetics of the potassium ion within the MOF nanocrystals compared to the phys. mixt. of MOF and rGO with almost the same microscopic morphologies.  As a result, such an MOF-rGO hybrid with strong interfacial chem. couplings delivered an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 422 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, superior rate performance (202 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), and outstanding long-term cycling performance (an ultralow decay rate of 0.013% per cycle after 2000 cycles at 2 A g-1), which are not only significantly better than those of the phys. mixt. of MOF/rGO but also among the best for anodes for PIB reported thus far.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpSwJ0KQ96VVLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHM38wUYPq8Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVSmsLrF&amp;md5=8885ee3d3b122accf6298ea9727d05bd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c07658"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, X.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-Organic Framework-Derived Nitrogen-Doped Cobalt Nanocluster Inlaid Porous Carbon as High-Efficiency Catalyst for Advanced Potassium-Sulfur Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Xiaoli; Di, Haoxiang; Wang, Peng; Miao, Xianguang; Zhang, Peng; Wang, Huiyang; Ma, Jingyun; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite high theor. capacity and earth-abundant resources, the potential industrialization of potassium-sulfur (K-S) batteries is severely plagued by poor electrochem. reaction kinetics and a parasitic shuttle effect.  Herein, a facile low-temp. pyrolysis strategy is developed to synthesize N-doped Co nanocluster inlaid porous N-doped carbon derived from ZIF-67 as catalytic cathodes for K-S batteries.  To maximize the utilization efficiency, the size of Co nanoparticles can be tuned from 7 nm to homogeneously distributed 3 nm clusters to create more active sites to regulate affinity for S/polysulfides, improving the conversion reaction kinetics between captured polysulfides and K2S3/S, fundamentally suppressing the shuttle effect.  Cyclic voltammetry curves, Tafel plots, electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, and d. functional theory calcns. ascertain that 3 nm Co clusters in S-N-Cos-C cathodes exhibit superior catalytic activity to ensure low charge transfer resistance and energy barriers, enhanced exchange c.d., and improved conversion reaction rate.  The constructed S-N-Cos-C cathode delivers a superior reversible capacity of 453 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 after 50 cycles, a dramatic rate capacity of 415 mAh g-1 at 400 mA g-1, and a long cycling stability.  This work provides an avenue to make full use of high catalytic Co nanoclusters derived from metal-org. frameworks.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdXXrDuiRB-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHM38wUYPq8Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1Kgsr3N&amp;md5=18b2e49f625985194ce423f015785641</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/D0NR00964D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Finding new org. materials to address several issues (e.g. capacity, stability, and cycle life) in org. potassium-ion batteries (OPIBs) is very important and highly desirable.         </div><div class="casAbstract">As a new class of cryst. porous materials, metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) have received great attention owing to their unique advantages of ultrahigh surface area, large pore vol. and versatile applications.  Developing different strategies to control the morphol. and size of MOFs is very important for their practical applications.  Recently, micro/nanosized MOFs have been regarded as promising candidates for electrode materials with excellent performances, which not only bridge the gap between fundamental MOF science and forward-looking applications, but also provide an opportunity to make clear the relationship between morphologies and properties.  This review focuses on the design and fabrication of one-, two- and three-dimensional MOFs at micro/nanoscale, and their direct applications in batteries, supercapacitors and electrocatalysis.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Progress of Nanoscale Metal-Organic Frameworks in Synthesis and Battery Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhong, Ming; Kong, Lingjun; Zhao, Kun; Zhang, Ying-Hui; Li, Na; Bu, Xian-He</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  As one type of promising inorg.-org. hybrid crystal material, metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) have attracted widespread attention in many potential fields, particularly in energy storage and conversion.  Recently, effective strategies have been developed to construct uniform nanoscale MOFs (NMOFs), which not only retain inherent advantages of MOFs but also develop some improved superiorities, including shorter diffusion pathway for guest transportation and more accessible active sites for surface adsorption and reaction.  Additonally, their nanometer size provides more opportunity for post-functionalization and hybridization.  In this review, recent progress on the prepn. of NMOFs is summarized, primarily through bottom-up strategies including reaction parameter- and coordination-assisted synthesis, and top-down strategies such as liq. exfoliation and salt-template confinement.  Addnl., recent applications of NMOFs in batteries as electrodes, separators, and electrolytes is discussed.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-organic framework derived N-doped CNT@ porous carbon for high-performance sodium- and potassium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Gaofei; Wang, Huanlei; Zheng, Yulong; Zhang, Hao; Yang, Yunpeng; Shi, Jing; Huang, Minghua; Liu, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering the lack of lithium resources, sodium- and potassium-ion storage systems possess great potential for large scale energy storage.  However, the slow charge storage kinetics of graphite hinders the intercalation of large sodium and potassium ions, leading to low capacity and poor cycling stability.  Herein, we report a nitrogen-doped carbon nanotube coated porous carbon derived from the metal-org. framework precursor for boosting the sodium and potassium ion storage.  The carbon product tested as anode deliverers a high specific capacity of 320/339 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1 in sodium/potassium ion batteries.  Ex-situ X-ray diffraction studies indicate that the dominant charge storage mechanism in the carbon is based on adsorption, rather than intercalation.  In addn., kinetics anal. further confirms that the capacitive-controlled capacity is dominant in the carbon electrode.  To further illustrate the merits of metal-org. framework derived nanoporous materials, hybrid sodium and potassium ion capacitors are assembled by using the carbon anode and cathode both from metal org. frameworks.  A high energy d. of 118/126 W h kg-1 can be achieved for sodium/potassium ion capacitors.  The present work provides a new strategy to design nanostructured carbons for high-performance metal-ion capacitors based on earth-abundant metals besides lithium.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrBwu_DaZ7oirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhTNNv7u-GRzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtlGjtLbP&amp;md5=8acdce5a3eeadebfa2e36c926fb08200</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.9b01127"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-Dimensional Ordered Macroporous Metal-Organic Framework Single Crystal-Derived Nitrogen-Doped Hierarchical Porous Carbon for High-Performance Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Xuefeng; Chen, Lanlan; Zhang, Wenhua; Wang, Jiawei; Liu, Zhenjie; Zeng, Sifan; Xu, Rui; Wu, Ying; Ye, Shufen; Feng, Yuezhan; Cheng, Xiaolong; Peng, Zhangquan; Li, Xifei; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
